BlargX
Well, Blazz, I'm not constantly referring to raiders being all lazy -- I am pointing out how the constant glory I hear raiders giving themselves is often pretty far-fetched. Since that outlook is said maybe 0.02% of the time whenever people talk about raiders versus casuals, and the opposite is said basically universally, it bears mentioning. When raiders stop making blanket statements about how hard raiding is or how skilled you have to be, and especially using that as the basis to assert that raiders should not get just better gear than casuals but gear with 3x, 4x, 5x and more the hitpoints etc -- then I call bull---er, baloney sometimes. Somebody has to.

Like I already did reply to someone else, the opposite understanding is the one that's taken for granted as though it were received religion from the mouth of god himself. It's hardly necessary for me to reiterate raider's praises for themselves when they've already put in years worth of effort on it, and the understanding that raiders are great, skillfull, hard-working players is pretty much the common one and taken completely for granted as it is.

By the way, I've never had a "Why raid" rant, though I know you're referring to the post where I asked why people who are supposed to like raiding always have to ask why they're supposed to do what they are busy saying they LIKE doing. My rants are more, "Why ONLY raid."

And I think it's poor game design when the answer remains, "Because it's the only way to progress."

Oh, also, Blazz, I've been in a pick-up raid organization for well over a year, and it's completely open. We started from the bottom with people who didn't even have any ornate, and now are trying PoP gods -- we got Fennin twice, missed on Xegony. There are indeed solutions that don't require being in a guild or raid organization that compels you to spend X hours per week. But...we can't forget that those are still not the norm on all the servers. Most guilds are very competitive, not cooperative, and most guilds and raiding organizations attempting much in the way of raiding at all absolutely require a certain number of hours per week, or that if you're online, you're raiding. Your guild is an exception among raiding guilds; mine is not. If you're going to get gear, it started out first as mere randoms, then added in merit sometimes or gear going toward the classes it was best for and now has moved on to DKP. In all cases but randoming gear, which is pretty silly at an advanced level, if you want your crack at the loot, you had better show up, and show up plenty.

There are theoretically alternatives, but not everyone has access to them. So we can't fairly speak about people having access to your type of guild or my type of organization as if they did -- we don't know whether they do or don't.

Most don't.

And because of that, the issues most of those people address remain valid -- without really being a committed raider, they don't have substantial avenues for significant improvement, and the number of useful zones they ever get in many of the expansions they pay for is minimal, and has grown extremely slowly. The expansions still remain geared toward other than the level 65 casual player to a very unbalanced extent.
BlargX
I have to admit I'm not fond of no-drop spells. But I'm not very sympathetic to people who don't buy their spells either. That's what I did for almost all my spells. I wasn't lucky enough to have many drop, or wasn't in the position(or flagged right) to get most of my spells as drops.

I earned them the other way you can earn them. I tradeskilled from virtually no plat at all, slowly but surely, through baking and brewing and then pottery and then smithing, with some SoW potions thrown in, to slowly build up a plat base. I camped stuff by myself, with a friend or two, and built up organized "camping associations" with an bunch of people where whoever was on that day of the missing classes would meet regularly and camp stuff, then all split the money from the stuff we all sold. Worked like gangbusters because EVERYONE got paid, not just one guy who did no more work than anybody else getting rich while all the others got jack for all their hours of work. It's a model that requires trust, but it's sooo much better than rolling and leaving most people feel used and broke while others hit the lottery. You knew you were going to get PAID.

I did this from Kunark through PoP, over and over again, starting from zero over and over again too.

I also took time whenever I could, when a new expansion came out, to try to find out where the phat lewt zones were before they got nerfed. I was striking out in Gates, but then recently spent some time in the arena in Gates and made 600k in a week.

That spells should be difficult to get, I'm not in agreement with, unless they make melee disciplines first just as important and secondly make them droppable on the same loot tables as caster spells. And I still think it's not a good idea.

That people at level 65 in this game can't scrape together 30 or 40k -- I understand the misery of accumulating plat, but really, I've been so broke in this game and come back from zero with no connections to help out so many times, from lower levels even, that my sympathy is very limited. Heck, you can make $1,500 an hour in the twilight sea, and $1k an hour just hunting spider silks in East Karana. And that's not really farming tough stuff; that's killing trivial stuff. You can go camp the piggy in tactics for drops that can still sell, sometimes for 5k or twice that on my server. You can very often buy hides and spiderling silk in the bazaar, simply combine them(very low tailoring skill), and then auction off the leather padding or just put it on a bazaar mule -- or ask to put it on a friend's bazaar mule and have him sell it for you.

Money can be annoying to get, sometimes risky to get, often boring to get, often time consuming to get, but it is not out of reach for a level 65 character, especially one who can solo greenies and light blues as easily as we can.

So as long as we're talking about spells, I'm all for having them not be such a pain to get; but with the existing system of them being droppable, you can get all the important ones indirectly, just by making some plat. It isn't all that hard to do at 65; it's pretty darn easy really. And those spells are cheaper than ever. I bought almost all mine when they were at top dollar, every time. Sometimes you have to do what it takes to get what you want.

Aemon Talishan
Any game system with progression will have an amount of have's and have-nots. At just about any time in your progression you will be looking at people that have things that you can not attain at that time.

A

I have no problem with different progressions for different people. When I get to the point where I've done the single-group content I want to see, I'll join a raiding guild. I'll most likely do so beforehand.

I also have no problem with itemization progression. There are two fairly distinct progressions of items in the game: the "casual" progression and the "raider" progression. The two paths are divergent and seem to be so out of necessity. The high-end raiding toons need vastly superior gear to handle the vastly more difficult content. The casual toons don't hit content of that magnitude and so don't need that gear. As EQ as a game has progressed, that divergence has become more pronounced, but it has always been there. I don't have a big problem with it because rarely am I in a situation where my gear is vastly inferior to what I need, as is the case for most players not engaged in high-end content.

My problem, as I said before, is spells. The concept introduced in Kunark and tweaked in PoP was to make some spells available only through encounters. Here's the issue:

Virtually all Kunark content is generally available to anyone, even what was at the time, high-end content (VS, Trakanon, etc.) As a result, the casual player has had the spells that drop from those areas become available to him because of the gradual increase in power of all gear. Velious and Luclin are generally the same, each had it's high-end keyed dungeon, but most other content was available to everyone, including mobs that dropped high-end spells (barring some Ancient stuff).

Enter PoP. No longer is it a keyed dungeon, it's an entirely keyed expansion. Further, the stuff hiding behind those keyed doors is several orders of magnitude harder than comparable encounters in previous expansions. As I said before, that is the result of the divergence in progressions between casual and raider play-styles.

But now, standard spell progression is thrown for a loop. For the first time, high-level (not high-end) spells are tied to generally inaccessible content. What about Fo7 warrants it only dropping runes in Tier 4+ (or Tier 3 named) when FoSoul can be gotten in Tier 1 from random spawns? Nothing about Fo7 (or BoS or Quiessence or Malos for that matter) warrants it being tied to extreme high-end content. By extreme, I mean content that will not likely ever be on the casual player's progression. The mobs that drop runes are not the kind of mobs that will be 2-3 group content like Trakanon is (for casuals, 1 groupable for EP+). It took several expansions to get casual players to where they are relative to Trakanon or Halls of Testing. PoP content is many orders of magnitude beyond that.

I agree that one doesn't NEED all of their respective classes spells. But at the same time, there is nothing about level 65 spells that warrants the effort required to get them. These spells are not of the same caliber as Time's Antithesis or Shinai of the Ancients or Raex Chestplate of Destruction. They don't even stack up to a Windblade, but many cost just as much:

Focus of the Seventh -- essentially a convenience spell. it adds nothing to Focus of Soul other than a group cast. about 50k on Prexus.
Blood of Saryrn -- shamans have been (justifiably) complaining plenty about the uselessness of Poison DoTs. 30-50k on Prexus
Malos -- -10 more to resists over Malo. a straight-line upgrade, and relatively minor at that. 15-20k on Prexus
Quiessence -- The only one of the bunch that I really would like, but still not so much better than Torpor that it warrants being a raider exclusive. Anywhere from 40-80k on Prexus
Ferine Avatar -- Really the only one that seems more appropriate for the raiding crew, despite its useless stat increases (except atk) for that group of folks. No idea on the price; I've never looked.

And for the many that say there is a path we are just not chosing to take it. As most have figured out, these are two distince debates.

Spells and Gear.

I think ALL people should have access to the spells, given enough time (ldon), PP (farming) or Raiding (dropped).

Gear, the elementals can have better gear until I get to the elementals in my own time. You can overcome lack of gear with playing skill with most classes. You can't overcome a spell that isn't in your spellbook and the content is tailored with the assumption that you DO have it.

If they don't make spells droppable, then the people that aren't flagged now will not be flagged next month, or the month after that. With no new tools, and without joining a raiding guild, people will have no better chance to get flagged and get better gear tomorrow than they have today.

Blazz, you are merely going into pit bull mode because the current game design suits you well. I understand that point. You've made it clear.

And certainly if everyone adjusted their style to be like you, and managed to get into EP+ raiding guilds that are fine with folks playing 10 hours a week, then you could pat them on the back for being inteprid and virtuous and, coincidentally, just like you.

The issue is the game used to be more flexible in design of progression. It's not now. Folks who don't raid are very quickly slammed to the end of their progression path. They get frustrated, whether they are play 40 hours a week or not, because they will not progress at remotely the same pace as someone who puts in LESS time but who gloms onto a raiding guild.

It doesn't need to be this way. This is weak game design. It can be better and these guys should be called onto the carpet for it.

I agree with the concept that those who raid should end up with better stuff. But those who raid should raid because they like raiding, and that is a form of reward itself. The degree of reward for raiding is way out of kilter with a sensible game design, in my view, and it's poisoning the game.

They can do better.

Raiders did better progression-wise in Kunark too, and yet the gulf was nothing like it is now. A smart, intrepid non-raider could keep pace to some extent. That's not true anymore, by a long long long margin. And it's going to get a lot worse, in a steep sloping line, if this trend is not significantly addressed.

At least, if I were a developer I would be pretty concerned.

i agree with this 100%. if you are that VERY rare person that plays 40 hours a week but loathes raiding, then, do it once, get flagged, and you're done. i hated GoD trial content but you don't see me posting flames to sony about them wasting my money and forcing me into a playstyle i didn't want (i prefer to raid) to play. but i think a lot of you are overreacting to the problem, as i agree w/ blazz in this that the vast majority of people we're discussing as being behind etc. are the "casual raider". then again, these are the people that put the least amount of time into the game, hence they have the longest timespan of "stuff to do" before they get bored and move on, so they SHOULD be behind. to imply that every raider is a talentless wheelcleric_01 and that every non-raider is a hard working and downtrodden individual is nuts and simply wrong. there are tards in raiding guilds, and there are tards who are guildless and don't like to raid.

everquest is/has been a raiding game since kunark. virtually every expansion has had content geared towards the raider and his guild. why now, all of a sudden, has this become such a ridiculous issue to cry over? because planes of power has been completed and instead of having 1 high end zone it has 10? because endgame pop gear is significantly better than endgame gear of the previous expansions? if you think hitting a road block of content in BoT when you hit 65 is an issue, try having nothing else to do but farm PoTime for the last year+ due to simply a lack of anything else to do. let's face it, when you put LOTS of time into the game, many of the flaws start to show. those of us that do, the raider and non-raider alike, will BOTH run out of stuff to do and get bored. and i agree with blazz, no one here has given me any good reason to make equal rewards for 1grpable content be it gear or zone access. i would be willing to bet, that the number of high playtime non-raiders with more playtime than the average raider is very, very small. so we have a very small group whining about why they should get equal rewards for NOT doing equally challenging content (if there were 1grpable it could not be as hard by simple game logistics)?

my logic is simply this: everquest is set up and has been set up for years as a raiding game. the flags/keys are there, if you want them. the game requires different playstyles in different situations to accomplish your goals. sometimes its a timesink (vt shards), sometimes its a raid (fennin/xegony/coirnav/rathe), sometimes its single grp trials (justice trials/GoD trials), but all and all zone access, which is one of the things being most highly debated here, DOES TAKE DIFFERENT TYPES OF PLAYSTYLES THAN MANY ARE COMFORTABLE WITH. i absolutely hated doing emp key stuff in ssra with a single grp. i did it, spent many hours there, got my key done, helped the rest of the grp get theirs, and moved on. would the game even be a challenge if it catered to the playstyle that everyone preferred? of course i was never a fan of needing 10+ clerics in a 72 person raid to win encounters, but then again, this was another challenge of the game, and it was very fun killing tallon zek and vallon zek the first time and getting to tier5 first.

true casuals are in great shape, if you don't/can't put a lot of time into this game like many of us can/shouldn't do heh, there is all sorts of stuff to do, whether it be exp, aa, quests, etc. i think you all are exaggerating just how many hardcore non-raiders there are. and i've said it before i'll say it again, there are plenty of ways to get flagged without a raiding guild. what is wrong at all with treating flags like keys that have to be done a certain way and then move on? it was that way in past expansions, and i treated it accordingly, with a "not fun but has to be done" mindset. seriously, as there are a TON of unguilded/family guild people flagged for the elemental planes as my server, i don't understand how this system has enraged so many. at the very least there are plenty of people flagged for a number of different zones past tier1. kunark required a raid to get into VP. velious required a key from a raid to get into ST. luclin required a raid to get into VT. and pop required raids to see the endgame content. nothing new here, just because there are multiple tiers of zones doesn't mean they are inaccessible to you because you hate raiding, nor does that mean that you should swear off all people that do choose to follow the progression path that's there. do i think they need to release another ldon type expansion or beef up ldon gear? yup, i do. i thought it was balanced decently against time gear, but from what i've seen of GoD gear non-raiding gear needs another boost. completely changing an expansion and the way it was set up, after many have adapted their playstyle to progress, would be silly. level 70 will solve a ton of the problems of non-raiders with regards to PoP, it will completely trivialize it. just like 65 did for luclin.

I have never denied that non-raiders outnumber raiders. But one thing I will argue STRONGLY against is that people seem to think that SOE is constantly releasing content aimed solely at raiders. Once there, the loot is better than EPs.

You say all they cater too is raiders. I say they are TRYING to cater to the more casual players as well. LDoN wasnt a raid expansion. LoY wasnt a raid expansion. Even Gates isnt SPECIFICALLY designed for raiding, despite all these threads and posts of people whining about how hard it is...

I do agree that the extra 5 levels will simplify all content. In fact, I agree with earlier threads guessing that GoD and OoW were initially one expansion...I just think they released them in the wrong order :p . As it is now, GoD isn't a "raiding" expansion, but you need to have been a raider in a previous expansion to be effective there (although this has lessened somewhat with the retooling.)

I also think a lot of the pushback we are seeing is around the game design approach of requiring flags for a majority of new content. This is an extremely frustrating situation for those of us that are not in guilds capable of completing flagging encounters. Yes, I can do tons of PU raids and eventually I'll get flagged, but that is incredibly frustrating - much more frustrating then it is for those people in a large raiding guild that can muster a competent force that's worked together on previous raids. If the current flag system had options for an equal amount of 2 to 3 group raids that would be fine because my guild could get that many 65's together and I know we know what we are doing on a raid. Unfortunately, that option does not exist.

The end result of the current flagging system for me is, if I don't want to put up with tons of failed PU raids, I won't be able to see EP+ content for another year or two. On the one hand that gives me a long term progression path, but on the other hand, I'm not going to buy any more expansions where I can only use a small percentage of the new zones.

By the way, yes, I could switch guilds, but I really like the people in the guild I'm in. So, for me, switching guilds is not an option I'll take.

jdthomas
Thinking about it, the whole ancient spell system is a good idea, just poorly implemented. Take the basic spell lineup and add a few ancients, with 10-15% more added. More heal, more nuke, whatever. The important thing is to not balance the class around them. They should be purely upgrades for those who put in the time. A little gloss is good, walling needed spells behind ancients is bad.
Who says there should be only one avenue for spells though? I see a lot of discussion on the best way to distribute spells. Shouldn't they be available as a drop, and as a point type purchase, and a turn-in, or whatever? Just so there is more than one way to attain the spells (not ancients). This would help to get people their spells in whatever way they are able, time wise. Perhaps this would perhaps prevent spell blocking/hoarding as well. Much of what this game is missing is the whole idea of multiple paths/similar result.
Predicus
I have been playing EQ now for about 4 years. I started playing back during Kunark, but really didn't get into the game until Velious. It wasn't until Luclin came out until I had a character over 30. It wasn't until PoP that I had a character over 55. I had been 65 for about 2 months before LDoN came out. Where am I going with this?

Everquest is a long-term game, it is one people have enjoyed for years. You can tell immediately upon logging in- it used to take forever to get back into the game. For a brand new player it takes quite some time to get to level 65, but we see very few arguments like this one over "Why do I have to be 65 to get cool gear?" Its a general consensus by casuals and hardcore alike that you level to 65. Raiders get better gear than non-raiders- this is a fact. There are some shamans out there that are close to/have broken 7k hitpoints unbuffed. These same shamans have been in Time for over a year- One zone/one year.

Everquest is a game of time- how much you have, and what you do with it. The more time you have and the better use of it- the better and faster you will progress. Everquest HAS always been this way. There are different aspects to the game- some suck, some suck worse. If you chose to disregard an aspect of the game, then you lose out on the positives and the negatives that come from it. It you choose not to level- then you don't, but don't complain that X player did and can now do Y. If you choose not to raid- then don't, but don't complain that X player did and can now do Y.

If SOE was to come out tomorrow and say "we are putting Time quality gear on LDoN merchants, but the content will be scaled to mirror difficulty of PoTime and you will not be able to complete the gear line without a year's worth of work"- players would baulk at it. That 7k shaman- whether good, bad, or mediocre has been farming the one zone of "progression" for over a year. Many still are, because many guilds are having to reflag and regear new players to replace those that left. SOE puts out more non-raid content zones than they have ever put out raid zones. Currently PoP has 12 "non-raid zones" with 1 zone that requires a groupable quest to access. PoP has 7 "raid-only" access zones, and PoP is considered a "damn raid expansion". GoD offers Natimbi, Quinimi, Barindu, Ferubi, Riwwi, 4 sewer trials, Vxed, Tipt to the non-raider and Kod'taz/Ikkinz if you are feeling especially freaky.

I am tired of hearing "but I am limited to one zone". It happens to everyone eventually, certain zones just yield better rewards than others. What I like to look for on posts are magelos- because it gives me an idea of where that person is at "content/progression-wise." If you are sitting around 4-4.5k unbuffed as a non-raid shaman- then you are done, good luck with wherever you choose to go. If you are sitting around 2.5-3k unbuffed- you are not, but you do have a choice. If you feel that Everquest is too much of a time sink- then you are done, good luck with wherever you choose to go. If you still want to play and progress- then do your research, a non-raid shaman can hit 4-4.5k unbuffed with group content/quests.

The usual retort to all of this is that "at my own pace I can get 65, I can't do the same with zone progression." In time everything becomes trivial to the point that when the difficulty gets low enough to the point that you want. Everquest has never been about equality- if it was we wouldn't have spawn times, rare drops, rare named, etc. The game has never been tuned this way, and coming in "five years later" and complaining about "equality issues" is pointless. The people that play more will get more. The people that follow the path set before them will progress faster. If I don't want to level to 65 then I don't deserve to cast level 65 spells. If I don't want to raid, then I don't deserve raid gear. I don't need raid gear to complete the current group content that I am in, so it's not an issue for me.

For those that say they don't have time to progress, I am really sorry but that is how the game was designed. In a progression-based game, there is absolutely no way to balance the progression of casual/non-casual players without trivializing someone's accomplishments. For those that are coming to the realization that EQ is a timesink, where were you the first 64 levels? Did you think the game was going to change once you dinged 65? Raiding is part of EQ's design. It is not required for those than want to progress to 65, it is designed to allow players to continue past 65 with more content. If you choose not to partake in this content, then do not expect the same rewards. If you do not have the time to partake in this content, then again I am sorry, but I think you need to find a game that fits better with your schedule.

The driving point that has made EQ the game that it is, is that it reflects life and allows enough personality to bleed through the bites of info to keep people coming back. There are games out there with better graphics, better game design, and better game play. People come back to see: xxxx the lazy cleric, yyyy the loot whore shaman, zzzz the cool warrior, and qqqq the nice rogue. It has created boards that debate issues that, on the surface, are game issues, but when you dig deeper represent similar issues that we see everyday in life. That is why people have played EQ for five years- not the graphics, not the loot, not the difficulty. EQ in many ways shows both the joy and monotony of life.

Wrapping this up- its getting long, but this issue will honestly never be resolved. Everyone on this board is using "flawed" logic in proving their side of the point. Logic relies on an objective individual witnessing a behavior and devising logic/law from it. No one here is objective to this issue- we each have our own side and are biased to it. Finally, in response to Absor's post and to those that posted a reply to it. Absor is one guy, as he pointed in numerous times in his posts. He is entitled to his opinion whether good or bad. He also pointed out that his opinion is not shared by SOE, and this was further proven by Brenlo's post to disregard it as SOE's vision. The final decisions on what SOE's vision is- lies solely on SOE, not Absor. To denounce an entire game on what one person's opinion (that is not shared by the company) is....stupid.

It is obviously shared by a lot more than just Absor based on their record, even if he is not an official spokesman. Considering how few and far between communications between the player community and SOE employees have been, it's refreshing to get such candor on their view of the game even unofficially.

All kidding aside, I'm still waiting for someone from SOE to state officially, on the record, what their thoughts on progression for the non-raider actually are. If it's Absor's opinion that's perfectly valid and I'll accept it- just stop saying one thing on your boxes while everyone who plays knows it's another.

Put the comments of Absor, Blazz or Predicus (to just pick 3) on ANY future expansion box and let's see how well it sells. Seriously- I dare you.

If EQ started off the way it is now, it would have crashed and burned almost immediately. How many old-timers joined EQ because they wanted to become hardcore raiders, with all that used to imply and still implies to a certain extent, or even concentrate mainly on raiding? In a world with few alternatives to raiding anywhere remotely as plentiful or well-designed? In a world where so much of the content you pay for is off-limits due to flagging/keying and the associated things that go with it?

I'd be willing to bet the percentage is absolutely VANISHINGLY small.

It's no accident that the game was never put together that way in the first place. Only a fool would have tried to sell a game like that, and only a bigger fool would have financed it.

There's no way that game would have sold nearly as well or lasted as long, 3D world or not, persistent world or not. If EQ was honestly marketed today or back then as exactly what it is right now, sales to new customers and sales of expansions both would plummet, and most of us wouldn't be here to see it, because the game would have shriveled to a withered shadow of what it is now long before today.

Iz is right on this one. I dare Sony to advertise honestly. But they know better than that. No chance in hell that will ever happen.

"Put the comments of Absor, Blazz or Predicus (to just pick 3) on ANY future expansion box and let's see how well it sells. Seriously- I dare you."

Izmalis is 100% on the money on this. EQ is consistently misrepresented in its advertising before you buy and its communications with customers afterwards as a game with an enormous amount of content for everyone.

I will definitely agree with you on this. EQ expansions have been misrepresented- I think its a combination of "spin-doctoring" by the PR guys and a lost sense of communication by the devs/players. GoD, as an expansion, was an utter disaster for all players. Cookie cutter mobs/zones with gear drops that make absolutely no sense on risk vs. reward. (You do a group trial and get EP level gear; you do a quest event requiring Time peeps and the gear drops are BoT tower quality.)

The GoD revamp should have been implemented before it went live, and loot tables still need to be looked at. They should have never released the expansion along with the DX9 patch- the combination killed a lot of active players.

As far as content goes, I preferred the all-in-one yearly expansions. They tend to provide something for everyone, and we have less of the X expansion was made for Y group. I think the biggest problem we have now is that most of the playerbase is 50+, and burnout comes often for everyone. Raiding was the answer in the past for those that burned through content, but doesn't work as well now. Basically, the bottleneck is getting smaller and tighter. SOE can't fall back on levels anymore to slow down people, and the current answer: flagging/keying isn't making people happy.

At the very least, we are getting feedback and SOE are starting to make some babysteps to fix long-standing issues. Its not going to be fixed in a week's time- there is too much, but I will be happy if they at least put forth the effort to make EQ better.
izmalis
I see that as constructive criticism, and I applaude those that have given it. I have not seen that from you. You have pointed out what you see wrong with the game, but have not given any ideas on corrections.
Then you haven't been paying attention. Here's a quick recap:
1- eliminate the design philosophy that most zones in an expansion must be raid flagged and "unlocked" just to access the content. This segregates the playerbase in what should be a social game.
2- reduce the gear gap to something even remotely close so that you don't have to design single group encounters around 2 sets of people, the raider and non-raider. The only way the non-raider will ever beat an encounter tuned for the raider is via mudflation several years and expansions down the road.
3- single group content and lots of it. Think Kunark. Improve LDoN- several good threads on this already.
4- Be up front and honest about your design philosophy for the game. If it's raid only, state that and be candid so there's no more misunderstanding and resentment based on false advertising.

Trevurg
1/3- I am all for more group content, but it needs to be varied and at the same time balanced. It does the Devs no good to release 10 new zones and have one give the best loots/xp. You just get 9 unused zones and 1 lagged out. Kunark was great, but pushing 60 I believe only Seb and maybe Howling Stones catered with xp content.

2- Narrowing the margin can be done, but you have to get the groupers out of PoP and LDoN. Those zones are very "comfortable" and I see a lot of today's players not wanting to cross a few zones to new content when BoT is "right next door".

Got 58 in Howling Stones - would have gotten it in Sky, but we finished clearing Isle 7 with me *this* close to 58 and nobody had remembered to spawn the Sister from bee isle so we couldn't get Sirran to spawn to get to 8.

Got 59 in the Hole - down near the undead tower was fantastic grinding. Could also pick off the basement named who was ALWAYS up and dropped two things a go. :) Can't remember his name now, was an erudite.

Granted, the Hole was opened pre Kunark but it was essentially a Kunark zone.

Got 60 in Chardok.

There were plenty of places to get to 60 - in my late 50s I got a lot of XP in Chardok, the second floor of City of Mist, doing the forager cycle... Deep Karnor's was all blue all the way to 60 and refreshingly clear of trains. I think I zoned into Sebilis for XP once, maybe twice, any other time was to farm spells from juggs or kill Trak.

Oooh! Plane of Hate, that was great XP and you walked out with SO much cash when you did it with one group. That was my first time treating an old raid zone as an xp zone. I even finally got the Rune Etched BP that had always eluded me on Hate raids.

There was a lot of great single group content. Of course, very few people used half of it - what you wound up with was swarms of people crowded into Sebilis complaining that there wasn't enough to go around - but it was designed so a group with some degree of insanity could go and do crazy things for fun. I had to buy a few coffins, I'll admit :)

There's a huge amount of single group stuff available today, and when I go out looking it's almost always unused and my group can take its pick of stuff to do.

People complaining about LACK of single group stuff to do are, I think, not complaining about the real problem - that is to say, the design in PoP where you take the most challenging single-group content that drops the best toys and gives the best xp and lock it behind a raid encounter. If Sol Ro and up were designed for raids only, I don't think you'd see half the frustration that PoP has engendered - this would be following the old model of

"Raid to get into Veeshan's Peak, where you pretty much just raid"
"Raid to get into Sleeper's Tomb, where you pretty much just raid"
"Raid to get into Vex Thal, where you pretty much just raid"

And not

"Raid to get into the elemental planes, where you can have lots of fun with five other people when you're not raiding"

Anyway, it's late, just thought I'd add more junk to an already huge thread.
Shabura Naarteban
I'll preface this by saying that I, personally, am a hardcore raider. My guild is fairly recently Time flagged. I have some Time gear. I'm Kod'Taz flagged, and hope to see Uqua in the near future, as well. By now, I'm sure several of the readers here have stopped to red-dot me, and won't read any further.

For those still with me, though ... I have several RL friends in the game. Some of them also raid. Many do not. I have (obviously) more free time than is healthy, and so I help them out with planning equipment that is available to them, when I can. Sometimes I take part in the kills - but I'm not so far above the curve that a non-raider shaman couldn't help in the places that I do.

There is this conception that a non-raider will be in total junk for equipment, and its one that I just don't understand. Maybe its the same reason I don't understand the "there is only one zone" approach to experience. Everyone claims how essential Fire (or Earth, depending on who is claiming) is to experience at the high end. I haven't spent more than two hours in those places, combined (other than raiding) in the last 2 months. My AA bar moves just fine. Likewise, there are plenty of drops available to the non-raider. Often, they are rare, or in out-of-the-way places. But they are there. And the fact that they might take some reading to learn about or some time to get makes them worthwhile - because it sets the one-group player who gets them apart from the hordes of barely-trained monkeys who think that Gaukr Sandstorm is the most excitement that one group can have in this game.

I don't have a one-group goal list set up for a shaman, because I don't have an RL shaman friend in that position. But I've got one for a ranger, and I'll use that as an example of what is available. (Almost) nothing on this list is a raid of any sort. Some of it is challenging to get, don't get me wrong. Keep in mind when you look at this, that the player this was intended for has been playing for a very long time (almost as long as I have), and this is by no means the first of these gear lists he has used as a goal sheet. Working your way up is easier than jumping to the top, after all.

Ear: Rhyolite Tear of Thralldom (http://lucy.allakhazam.com/item.html?id=68441) (random drop, Barindu)
Neck: Silvery Mesh Yunjo Sash (http://lucy.allakhazam.com/item.html?id=52093) (Riwwi quest)
Face: Chanting Stone Mask (http://lucy.allakhazam.com/item.html?id=68598) (random drop, Vxed)
Head: Polished Zraxthril Coif (http://lucy.allakhazam.com/item.html?id=40187) (Innoruuk, Crypt of Nadox) *
Ear: Polished Garnet Loop (http://lucy.allakhazam.com/item.html?id=68591) (Chavoor the Trickster, Vxed)
Finger: Turepta Spine Ring (http://lucy.allakhazam.com/item.html?id=68508) (random, one of the sewers)
Wrist: Silver Bracelet of Speed (http://lucy.allakhazam.com/item.html?id=31461) (Temple of Veeshan quest) **
Arms: Incorporeal Arms of the Specter (http://lucy.allakhazam.com/item.html?id=44309) (LDoN point buy)
Hands: Incorporeal Gauntlets of the Specter (http://lucy.allakhazam.com/item.html?id=44311) (LDoN point buy)
Wrist: Stone Bracelet of Battle Mastery (http://lucy.allakhazam.com/item.html?id=44293) (LDoN hard. Tradeable.)

(at this point, Lucy just went down ... if I remember, I'll edit this with links, later. If not, its not hard to look these up yourself. *grin* )

Finger: Ring of Dain Frostreaver IV (Coldain ring quest) ***
Shoulders: Mantle of Ferociousness (random drop, Ferubi)
Chest: Incorporeal Chain of the Specter (LDoN point buy)
Back: Cloak of the Sharp Eye (Umbiki, Vxed)
Waist: Sash of the Yunjo's Champion (Riwwi quest)
Legs: Seamless Spiked Leggings (Kyv Hunter, Vxed)
Feet: Boots of an Aged Mystic (LDoN hard. Tradeable.)

Primary/Secondary: I don't touch melee weapon selection. He's on his own here.
Ranged: Stonewood Compound Bow. (Elemental crafted. Tradeable.)

* This one is a raid drop, albeit from a small raid. It was an item that interested the player, and I'll be helping to put the event together. For the true non-raiding experience, sub in another piece of LDoN 1492 gear here - its almost as good, anyway.
** This one might be a 2-3 group raid for non-raid-geared players, not to mention the trick of finding Dozekar the Cursed actually alive. I've one-grouped him with very much non-raiding people in the other 5 slots, and I'd argue that a group of people equipped in anything even halfway close to this profile would drop him like a bad habit. Even so, its on the list mostly because its simply too good of an item for him NOT to try to get.
*** This is clearly a raid item. Rings 1-9 are soloable/duoable, however, and at least on my server, the population is usually amenable to pickup 10th ring wars. If your server is not so kind, or you just really want your gear to be raid-free, there are no shortage of solid rings. A rather nice one drops in Ferubi, and even the LDoN point buy Ring of Mold is reasonably good.

All told, the raw bonuses from gear are over 400 AC, around 1800 hp, and over 1500 mana. There are enough saves to put all this ranger's unbuffed saving throws to 120 or higher. It has 95 points of +ATK gear. It has 41% haste. It has FT 6. It even has a spell range focus and Plainsight. And this is before adding any augmentations at all. Is this hard to get? You're absolutely right it is. But its done without raiding. Heck, most of the people this player groups with aren't even people I know. They are other (many of them non-raiding) people he's met along the way, while farming for LDoN points, or eeking out groups in out of the way zones like Riwwi.

Every class in the game can look like this - or better - without raiding. And this ranger profile is frankly better than a lot of VT/early PoP level raiding rangers. Honestly, I think we have a ranger or two in my Time guild that doesn't match this profile for raw hp or armor class.

And ... its not like this is the end. This is just another upgrade chart. There have been perhaps a dozen before this, and there'll likely be that many after it. He doesn't always finish one before starting the next. This one likely will be no different (that Barindu earring is being particularly elusive at the moment), and he's thinking about backing out of doing the quest for the belt and neck. But you'll see there is no bracer off the Tipt boss on this list, nothing from Kod'Taz, or the one-group Ikkinz trials. That's next. I won't argue the difficulty of Tipt, KT, or Ikkinz. But dressed like this (or thereabouts), he'll be ready to try it. And because he's played with other people, been personable, and been willing to take the initiative some time, he's got a channel full of friends (about 5-10 on at their peak play times, in general - so I suppose they *could* do a 2-group-ish mini raid if needed) who will be willing to help get there with him, and who have similar goals and aspirations that don't need a 72 man raid to get them, or even a 18 man raid. They've already been learning how to kill mobs at the Vxed zone in without dying. I imagine they'll be beating it soon - quite possibly without me even along.

Sure, they'll never have the Elemental or Time drops that I'm wearing. But, you know what? I'd replace my Phase 1 Time mask with the mask that can drop off any mob in Kod'Taz. And this ranger, and his friends, will see Kod'Taz some day, and be able to loot that mask. Casual play has rewards, and they are almost as good as the rewards that we raiders enjoy. Its hard! Don't get me wrong. But I don't think its any harder than what a raiding guild member has to deal with - the drama of backflags and login numbers, of recruiting and guildhopping, of the 15% visa limit and Coirnav kills and Time rotations and ....

Oh ... and as a closing, to make this post germane to the original topic of this thread ... by the time they get to where they are going, this ranger and his friends will have all their spells except the Ancients (their friendly clerics may or may not wind up all having Divine Intervention, not sure yet). With the changes to GoD spells, that'll happen even faster.

Casual EQ. 1-group EQ. Its not dead (check out the amount of GoD stuff on that list!), and its not all doom and gloom. Its just not handed out free by logging in and grinding XP in BoT and hoping Oreen doesn't get trained to the 4-way (again).

Predicus
If you are equalling casual EQ with 1-group EQ I have to disagree. While it is commendable that you took time to list all these wonderful things that might be 1-groupable most of them are not realistic for a casual player.

Casual EQ at 65 might not be dead but it sure isnt exciting either.

Casual EQ is dead. Everquest was never designed to fit the casual player. Everquest has never catered to many market: young players, science fiction fans, shoot 'em up fans, sports fans. Does this make EQ a poor game? -only to those that wanted those aspects catered to them. EQ was designed around a D&D concept- a long, in-depth RPG for the teenager/young adult community that had ample free time and a semi-liquid income. Pointing this out this late in the game is like pointing out "hey, there's woodelfs in the game!"

SOE has put in many tools for those leveling from 1-65, but not to cater to the casual player. It catered to those that were becoming disgruntled with level progression, and to teach people of where to go to group and what to do/not to do. The one major side-effect that I see to this is that people leveled faster, and we have a lot of 65's who are used to the expedited pace. I see many 65 level players that: don't know where to go to make pp, don't know where X zone is, don't know how to get to Y zone without a port, don't want to go any farther than 2 zones away from PoK.

That is the problem I see with the game today. PoP trivialized the need to watch your butt and pay attention. PoP created the "semi-afk" player- there is no longer the thrill of keeping the group alive because if you don't- the group just pops back at the zone-in 15 minutes later. SOE has revamped many older zones, and they are EMPTY. I was in PoHate last night soloing, and I think I saw a total of 8 players over a 6 hour period. I see the same 6-8 players in Droga- I see 1-2 in Nurga. I see 2-3 in Chardokb, 4-5 in Chardok, and 0 in Siren's Grotto. The named spawn rate in Droga is ridiculous- I have literally made over 1000k in that zone, but I still go there because people will still pay 10k for a copper hammer of striking.

Players don't want to leave BoT, Raiders don't want to leave PoTime- that is the problem. We can sit here a post an itemized list of how to get a non-raid shaman to 5k unbuffed, and get baulked at because it can't be done unless people leave their comfort zone. There is content out there- stop hanging out by the waterhole.
UgZug
Non-raiding players will typically cap at BoT/HoH/Barindu-sewers.

For those zones, you require no raiding experience, only 5 friends and level 62-65.

In those zones, you can get runes (all PoP level 65 spells) as well as Balance of Nihil and Daluda's Mending.

That makes the only spells UNavailable to the non-raider to be Breath of Trushar and the Ancient spells (2 in high Luclin zones and 1 in high GoD). Of those 4 spells that you don't have access to one is a nearly useless poison dot, one is a totally worthless "upgrade" to avatar, one is a mediocre upgrade to Quiescence, and the last is a significant upgrade to Can4.

So, in review, with the exception of the Ancient Canni, what spells, exactly, do you feel like you don't have access to yet need?

Beyond that, what else do raiders get that non-raiding players don't? They get better zone access which provides them somewhat better exping grounds, better drops, progression.

For the non-raiding player who spends their time milking an AA per hour in BoT (not good enough for you?....) you do NOT need 7K hitpoints... you do NOT need the extra 5-10% on your focus effects... you do NOT need the progression... you just WANT it because you're jealous that other people have it and you do not.

Newsflash: the people that have it busted their asses for it. They have the gear, the flags, and the perks because they invested time AND money into doing it. You stating that you paid for the expansion means nothing till you can say you have put in the effort as well. You only have completed HALF of the quest... money is 50% of the process, folks... stop thinking that you are OWED something that you haven't earned.

The non-raiding players have whined so much that Sony had to give in and they openned up zones in PoP and made nice gear available in LDON... but that's not good enough for you... no... you want full access to everything without working for it. You want SolRo today... and you'll want Elemental/Time tomorrow... and a month after that it won't be good enough till you have Kod'taz or even Uqua access...

Stop bitching and earn your progression if it's so important to you.

Saar_Tribunal
I think there is a great deal of confusion going on here.

I never said I wanted access to “raid content” solo or with a single group.
I never said I wanted things to be easy, or handed to me. I have worked for everything I have in this game. No eBay or pp purchases.
I never said I wanted access to Time or some such.

What I have said I want is Progression.
Another good word would be Accomplishment.

That’s why everyone plays this game, only difference between players is what fulfills those things for us.

For some it is role-playing. For others it’s exploring. For others still it is the social aspects, making friends and spending time together.

Do you really think you raid to Raid? If so, you would hit the same targets night after night if there were NO loot drops, NO flags to get. You don’t, in fact you would quit overnight if you got nothing for your efforts.

I greatly enjoyed EverQuest for the progression I have had. A big thing for me is character development so improving my gear, getting skills, spells, AAs, etc. Well as a non-guild/non-raider I have no progression left. The top of the food chain for me is BoT. Level 65 shaman, 120 AA, all my level 65 spells. Heck it took me several months to save the cash to buy my spells. I did it, and then everything ended for me it seems.

What is left for me?

I could work on a full set of Ornate, though I cant single group all the drops. Buying it would be in the 600-800kpp range, or about 8-10 months of farming cash drops for me.

The other option is LDoN gear.
Approximately 5000 points per fully augmented piece of gear
About 1.5-2 hours per adventure (LFG time, setup time, adventure time)
51 points per adventure
That works out to be 150-200 hours of LDoN per piece of gear
For say 10 pieces of gear that’s up to 2000 hours to get a set
At 20 hours a week, that would be 2 years of playtime.

Does anyone think that is a reasonable Progression?

After all that work, what content do I play in? A handful of more zones?

A thing is worth what you pay for it. I don’t want anything handed to me.
I paid for my level 65 shm, in time and effort, now there is nothing left to work for.

Again I am grateful to Alan for posting the SOE “vision” for EverQuest. Knowing that things won’t be changing, and that the insight I have come to at level 65 is correct makes it much easier to be ending my billing.

I also want to thank Brenlo for posting here. While your statement that spells will be easier to acquire is welcome it wont help the over all issues for the non-raider.

Shabura Naarteban
Maybe I'm just dense, and don't understand what some of you want as a "casual player". I'm not trying to be patronizing here, honestly. I'm NOT a casual player ... I play 6 hours a day, on average, 6 days a week. I know what kind of player I am.

But then, someone posts here that the items I listed are impossible for a casual gamer to acquire. And I'm left wondering ... why not?

I am assuming that a truly casual player plays 2-3 hours per day, 2-4 days per week, but as nevertheless managed to get 65 + the really essential AA. How do you then progress? Make friends. There are always other people on. Do some crappy pickup groups for a week (I'd suggest LDoN over BoT to make this goal easier), and look for the people that are on regularly in your play window. Find a few that are competant and make friends. Set up a channel that you all autojoin. Plan some grouping. There are LOTS of great places in the game that are bring-your-own-group. This is how to get it!

Some of the items on that list take a lot of time to get. The random drops in GoD are really rare, and take days of killing. But they don't have to be all at once. Heck, I soloed for a Fractured Obsidian Band, 2 hours at a time. Took me a week or so. Its way easier with some friends. The drops from Vxed named? Yeah, they are nasty, but a chanter charm pet + weaponshield ranger makes one dead real quick - and requires no gear at all (some AA on the chanter is nice, true, but still...). If you're, say, farming Umbiki (who also drops Nihil, as a nod to the fact that this IS a shaman board), the time from zone-in to dead Umbiki can be as little as 15 minutes if you're lucky with the spawns. And that's not with an amazing, Time-geared group. I've done it with 4 people in 30 minutes, and of them I was the only one that had any raid gear on at all.

The last time I logged in, I went through GFay on my way to an LDoN, and some level 2 wood elf warrior sent me a tell asking if I "had any gear to give." I can't help but feel this casual gaming argument is like that wood elf. There's plenty of stuff out there, and its doable. But its not free. If casual gamers - especially ones that post on assorted boards lamenting casual gaming - spent that time looking at possible drops, making some in-game contacts, and taking some risks visiting new places, then they'd be in gear that looks like that list.

And if that level of equipment doesn't satisfy you, and you STILL don't want to raid ... then, yes, its probably time to find a new game. =P

Saar, I definitely agree with what you say- but you stopped at LDoN normal as it was the end of group progression. When I started doing LDoN normal- it was hard. People died routinely and there was a 50/50 chance that you would succeed. Now I enjoy doing LDoN hard, and rarely lose them. (damn low drop rate collects) The point I am trying to make is that you will get to the point where you can complete LDoN hards in the same amount of time as LDoN normals- thereby cutting your progress rate in half. On top of this there is GoD content where you can upgrade nearly every piece of gear you own. These items are superior to LDoN purchased items.

So the progression for non-raiders is:

LDoN normal/PoP- get a few pieces of ornate/ldon gear until content is
trivial.

LDoN hard- more points per win = faster progression/ldon hard dropped
items

GoD- GoD gear drop items to further hp/mana/focus effect/ft. Faster
collection of augments to cut ldon purchase cost.

A non-raid shaman can and will break 4.5k hitpoints if he follows this progression line. My guess is that, upon completion of Kod'taz farming, a non-raid shaman could be sitting at around 5.2-5.5k hitpoints.

Macheras
For those that say they don't have time to progress, I am really sorry but that is how the game was designed. In a progression-based game, there is absolutely no way to balance the progression of casual/non-casual players without trivializing someone's accomplishments. For those that are coming to the realization that EQ is a timesink, where were you the first 64 levels? Did you think the game was going to change once you dinged 65? Raiding is part of EQ's design. It is not required for those than want to progress to 65, it is designed to allow players to continue past 65 with more content. If you choose not to partake in this content, then do not expect the same rewards. Ignorance and apathy, quite a combination.

The reason that the gear is markedly different is that raiders couldn't survive many encounters without the extra hitpoints. The fact that they can solo mobs in lesser plains is just a side effect.

If I hear one more post about open up SolRo Tower I will cry. You lot don't want to be able to grind there because you get better xp in BoT. What you really want is to be able to wake up, rub your eyes, and see a pile of shiny ornate molds at your feet. There are currently three reasons to go to Sol Ro:

1) Ornate drops
2) Raiding
3) A quiet place to get away from the BoT crowd

I'd rather see ornate molds priced like water and put on every vendor than give up #3.

If they choose to open up the elemental planes to the non-raiding, casual, probably-plays-twice-as-much-in-a-week-than-I-do player I am fine with it. All I ask is that SoE give me 200aa on the day they do so. Not that I deserve 200aa (which is what I probably would have ground if I hadn't been raiding to progress and equip my character), but simply because if you guys get something for nothing I want the same.

Alternatively give a good, honest, unbiased, reason why you should get markedly better equipment without having to face elemental encounters and I'll change my opinion. Hang on, scratch that, I doubt I would.

Check out the named mobs in the Tipt/Vxed/Sewer trials. Some quick info, though:

Tipt: 2 named every trial

Enraged Cragbeast drops augs: 30hp/30end; 30hp/30mana; ft2/regen 2; regen 2/atk 15?

The cool thing about the hp augs is that they are slot all/all- really nice to plug them into 3 slot LDoN gear (check out my BP in my magelo)

Kyv Hunter Bob: drops 4 bracers and some sword- chain bracer has 140hps on it if I remember correctly

Vxed: a few drops for shamans (long trial folks)

Kyv Hunter Jim: drops 100hp/100mana chain legs

Ukun Bloodbeast: drops 90hp ring

Ikavv Something: drops 80hp belt?

Beluda angry mom: drops 120hp shield w/ EE4 (end boss-always up)

Barindu:

rare drop off common mobs: 100hp/100mana ft2 ring

noc something: drops 80hp boots?

Sewers: 80hp cloak, 100 hp belt, 100 hp earring

Basically, do some research on GoD zones. There are a lot of one-groupable drops out, and also a lot of augs. (Ferubi consistly yields 35hp/35mana/35end augs) Also, look at the drops from LDoN hards- the gear is out there.
